The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Install Plugin, version 2.5.2&#010;&#010;The Install Plugin is used during the install phase to add artifact(s) to the&#010;local repository. The Install Plugin uses the information in the POM (groupId,&#010;artifactId, version) to determine the proper location for the artifact within&#010;the local repository.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-install-plugin&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-install-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.5.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven Install Version 2.5.2&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MINSTALL-100] - Update description for installAtEnd param&#010; * [MINSTALL-103] - Concurrency problem with installAtEnd in parallel builds&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MINSTALL-106] - MavenProject/MavenSession Injection as a paremeter instead as a component.&#010; * [MINSTALL-107] - Upgrade to Maven 2.2.1 compatiblity&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Tue, 02 Sep 2014 06:40:49 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Deploy Plugin, version 2.8.2&#010;&#010;The deploy plugin is primarily used during the deploy phase, to add your&#010;artifact(s) to a remote repository for sharing with other developers and&#010;projects. This is usually done in an integration or release environment. It can&#010;also be used to deploy a particular artifact (e.g. a third party jar like Sun's&#010;non redistributable reference implementations).&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-deploy-plugin&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-deploy-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.8.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven Deploy Version 2.8.2&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MDEPLOY-172] - Concurrency problem with deployAtEnd in parallel builds&#010; * [MDEPLOY-174] - [REGRESSION] url not required anymore, causing a NullPointerException&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MDEPLOY-185] - MavenProject/MavenSession Injection as a paremeter instead as a component.&#010; * [MDEPLOY-186] - Upgrade to Maven 2.2.1 compatiblity&#010;&#010;Enjo&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
&quot;Robert Scholte&quot; &lt;rfscho...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Maven release plugin fail during javadoc generation  
Date  :-
Sat, 06 Sep 2014 10:02:23 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;the plugin causing this problem must be .... the maven-javadoc-plugin :)&#010;&#010;the release:perform isn't that magic, you can do the same steps by hand:&#010;- check out the code from tag (created by release:prepare)&#010;- go to target/checkout&#010;- execute "mvn deploy site-deploy" (site-deploy depends on the  &#010;availability of a site under distributionManagement)&#010;&#010;If you still have the target/checkout folder, run 'mvn site' and you'll  &#010;see your project failing for the same reason as you mentioned.&#010;&#010;There's a small difference between calling javadoc:javadoc and site. The  &#010;first one will only get its configuration from the javadoc-plugin as  &#010;specified in the build-section.&#010;However, if the javadoc generation is generated as part of the site phase,  &#010;the configuration is picked up from the reporting-section in the pom.xml.  &#010;This can lead to different results.&#010;&#010;Hope this helps you figuring out the real problem.&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Wed, 03 Sep 2014 09:22:33 +0200 schreef Sylvain Roulet  &#010;&lt;sylvain.roulet@eloquant.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello all,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've a project since several years and I had not problem to build it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I recently installed JDK1.7 on my Windows 7 and now my build fail during  &#010;&gt; mvn&#010;&gt; release:perform !&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The build fail saying "unmappable character for encoding utf-8".&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That's true as my source file are encoded in ISO-8859-1.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So I've added &lt;encoding&gt; ISO-8859-1&lt;/encoding&gt; =&gt; no change&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I try to use env variable : JAVA_TOOL_OPTIONS =  &#010;&gt; -Dfile.encoding=ISO-8859-1&#010;&gt; =&gt; no change&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;skip&gt;true&lt;/skip&gt; to not generate javadoc =&gt; no change...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; and a lot of other tests&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I finally realized that the option file generated in the folder&#010;&gt; /target/checkout/target/apidocs&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; contains options saying that encoding is UTF-8 !&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't think it is a maven javadoc plugin problem as if I run mvn&#010;&gt; javadoc:javadoc, I runs successfully !&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Finnaly if I use JDK 1.6 it runs perfectly... But that's not what I want  &#010;&gt; to&#010;&gt; do.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does any one have any idea why options are not taking into account when&#010;&gt; maven release:perform is executed&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
&quot;Trezise, Brian&quot; &lt;Brian.Trez...@inin.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Need file from src/main/resources in generate-sources phase for annotation processor config  
Date  :-
Wed, 03 Sep 2014 18:06:39 GMT  
contents:- 
I posted this question on StackOverflow but I’m stuck and haven’t been getting much response&#010;so I decided to go to the “source” as it were.&#010;Here’s a link to the question on SO, if you prefer to answer there (helpful answers will&#010;get up-voted, best answer accepted):&#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/25645944/need-file-from-src-main-resources-in-generate-sources-phase-for-annotation-proce&#010;&#010;The question:&#010;I have an annotation processor that I need to give some configuration to tell it a few details&#010;about how I want it to generate source code.  I spent a good deal of time trying to understand&#010;why the file was sitting in target/classes after the build, but I was getting an exception&#010;during annotation processing stating that the file did not, in fact, exist.&#010;&#010;After much digging I finally figured out why the file (stored in `src/main/resources/config`)&#010;isn't getting copied over to `target/classes/config` for my annotation processor to read -&#010;`generate-sources` happens before `process-resources` in the build lifecycle, so the file&#010;isn't getting copied over in time for the annotation processor to see it during its run. (maven&#010;build lifecycle reference: http://maven.apache.org/ref/3.2.2/maven-core/lifecycles.html)&#010;&#010;Here's a high level overview of what I'm trying to do:&#010;&#010;I have a jar that I've built that processes annotations and generates interface classes from&#010;the information in the annotations to base a client api off of.  The idea is that including&#010;that jar as a compile-time dependency should automatically generate this code for any project&#010;that uses these annotations (with as little-as-possible additional configuration in the client&#010;project's pom.xml).&#010;&#010;How do I go about either:&#010;&#010; 1. Getting (at a minimum) the config.xml portion of process-resources to happen before generate-sources&#010; 2. Adding the file to the classpath of the annotation processor in some other way (we don't&#010;need this file in the output archive, so this might be better)&#010;&#010;I would prefer not to write a whole maven plugin for this if possible.&#010;&#010;Here are the relevant parts of the `&lt;build&gt;` portion of my client pom:&#010;&#010;    &lt;build&gt;&#010;        &lt;finalName&gt;OurApp&lt;/finalName&gt;&#010;        &lt;resources&gt;&#010;            &lt;resource&gt;&#010;                &lt;!-- My config.xml file is located here --&gt;&#010;                &lt;directory&gt;src/main/resources&lt;/directory&gt;&#010;            &lt;/resource&gt;&#010;            &lt;resource&gt;&#010;                &lt;directory&gt;src/main/webapp&lt;/directory&gt;&#010;                &lt;includes&gt;&#010;                    &lt;include&gt;*.*&lt;/include&gt;&#010;                &lt;/includes&gt;&#010;                &lt;excludes&gt;&lt;exclude&gt;${project.build.directory}/generated-sources/**&lt;/exclude&gt;&lt;/excludes&gt;&#010; Subject  :-
Re: maven-dependency-plugin unpacking aar format?  
Date  :-
Thu, 04 Sep 2014 20:16:20 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi there,&#010;&#010;just my few cents...&#010;An artifact type is something quite central. IMHO it is not the best way &#010;to force all artifacts to keep the information how to unpack it in their &#010;POMs and then magically fiddle it out from there.&#010;&#010;If I type "mvn foo" and there is a maven-foo-plugin or foo-maven-plugin &#010;in the right groupId, then maven will automatically figure it out. So I &#010;would expect something similar here.&#010;&lt;packaging&gt;aar&lt;/packaging&gt;&#010;could trigger that some aar-maven-plugin is responsible for packaging. &#010;There could be a convenience goal for unpacking.&#010;&#010;If you want to have some proprietary packaging in some other namespace &#010;(and not available in central) there could be some hint configured in &#010;settings.xml.&#010;&#010;Cheers&#010;   Jörg&#010;&#010;Am 22.07.2014 19:41, schrieb Robert Scholte:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; to be able to unpack/unarchive Maven must know which Unarchiver should &#010;&gt; be used for this type. 'aar' is not one of the few default supported &#010;&gt; types, hence the exception.&#010;&gt; The plugin responsible for packaging the aar-file should also have &#010;&gt; configured how to unarchive the aar-file.&#010;&gt; In case of dependency:unpack it is quite simple: I would expect that &#010;&gt; the packaging plugin is configured in the pom.xml with a &#010;&gt; &lt;extension&gt;true&lt;/extension&gt;. This way Maven can find such information.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; However, I can imagine that in case of unpack-dependencies the &#010;&gt; aar-project.pom isn't used to detect the corresponding Unarchiver. &#010;&gt; Sounds like an improvement to me.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ps. this is also an interesting usecase for the consumer-pom or the &#010;&gt; flatten-maven-plugin&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Op Mon, 21 Jul 2014 22:40:18 +0200 schreef David Hoffer &#010;&gt; &lt;dhoffer6@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I'm getting the following error trying to unpack some files from an aar.&#010;&gt;&gt;  Is this not supported?  Is there any way to do this?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Failed to execute goal&#010;&gt;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-dependency-plugin:2.8:unpack-dependencies&#010;&gt;&gt; (unpack-service) on project service: Unknown archiver type: No such&#010;&gt;&gt; archiver: 'aar'. -&gt; [Help 1]&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; -Dave&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Apache Archiva 2.1.1 Released  
Date  :-
Fri, 05 Sep 2014 00:44:13 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Archiva team is pleased to announce the release of Archiva&#010;2.1.1. Archiva is available for download from the web site.&#010;&#010;Archiva is an application for managing one or more remote&#010;repositories, including administration, artifact handling, browsing&#010;and searching.&#010;&#010;If you have any questions, please consult:&#010;&#010;the web site: http://archiva.apache.org/&#010;the archiva-user mailing list: http://archiva.apache.org/mail-lists.html&#010;&#010;Apache Archiva 2.1.1 is a bugs fix release:&#010;&#010;NOTE: jdk 1.7 is now prerequisite with Apache Archiva 2.1.1&#010;&#010;Compatibility Changes&#010;&#010;If upgrading from earlier versions of Archiva, the list of libraries&#010;in wrapper.conf has changed. If you have customized your copy of&#010;wrapper.conf, please update it for compatibility with the version&#010;distributed with the current release.&#010;As the database storage has been removed, you can remove the JNDI&#010;entry for jdbc/archiva. After upgrading from a previous version, you&#010;will have to run a full scan to populate the new JCR Repository. This&#010;will be done on first start of Archiva.&#010;&#010;Refer to the Upgrading Archiva guide for more information.&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;&#010;Bug&#010;&#010;[MRM-1832] - RepositoryScannerTest#testDefaultRepositoryScanner fails&#010;on Linux with src release zip&#010;[MRM-1853] - On first start up, you get a perpetual loading indicator.&#010;[MRM-1854] - Last modified date is epoch on directory listing for a group&#010;[MRM-1855] - "Loading" button never disappears when no one is logged&#010;in in some browsers&#010;[MRM-1856] - archiva-cli does not work&#010;&#010;&#010;Have fun!&#010;-- &#010;The Apache Archiva Team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I just got this working with doxia:&#010;&#010;http://bramp.github.io/js-sequence-diagrams/&#010;&#010;Sequence diagrams are great for documenting protocol interaction.&#010;&#010;I use them very often but one of the problems is updating the document when&#010;the protocol changes.&#010;&#010;With text sequence diagrams you can do that easily…&#010;&#010;Here’s an example:&#010;&#010;Andrew-&gt;China: Says Hello&#010;Note right of China: China thinks\nabout it&#010;China--&gt;Andrew: How are you?&#010;Andrew-&gt;&gt;China: I am good thanks!&#010;&#010;… and that can be rendered into an image for every page load.&#010;&#010;I have it working in my doxia by just updating &lt;head&gt; and then using a &lt;div&#010;class=‘diagram’&gt;&#010;&#010;and then:&#010;&#010;$( document ).ready(function() {&#010;    $(".diagram").sequenceDiagram({theme: 'hand'});&#010;} );&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;&#010;Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;… or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&#010;

It's the proxy server that is returning the&#010;error.&#010;&#010;I know everything else is correct because if I set active=false, the deploy succeeds.&#010;&#010;Thanks&#010;&#010;John&#010;&#010;&#010;

Please check the URL you are&#010;trying to reach to verify that it is spelled correctly."&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This is in the log:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [INFO] Deploying war to http://localhost:8080/coherence-extend-web&#010;&gt; Uploading: http://localhost:8080/manager/text/deploy?path=%2Fcoherence-extend-web&#010;&gt; Uploaded: http://localhost:8080/manager/text/deploy?path=%2Fcoherence-extend-web (8409&#010;KB at 3024.7 KB/sec)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [ERROR] Tomcat return http status error: 404, Reason Phrase: Not Found&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That looks correct except the error isn't quite right because Tomcat isn't even being&#010;hit. Name  :- 
Matthias-Christian Ott &lt;...@mirix.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Build dependencies from source code  
Date  :-
Mon, 08 Sep 2014 21:59:56 GMT  
contents:- 
My current understanding is that Maven and Maven repositories are&#010;primarily used to distribute pre-compiled binaries and to build other&#010;software against these binaries. I want to build all dependencies of a&#010;project from source code.&#010;&#010;I found that it is possible to publish source code through Maven&#010;repositories and build dependencies that provide source code via the&#010;source, dependency and build helper plugins. However, despite some&#010;technical problems (non-incremental builds, no separate .jar files), it&#010;seems this is not how Maven is normally used for.&#010;&#010;Some Linux distributions also build all software that uses Maven from&#010;source and have developed their own software to isolate Maven builds and&#010;build them only with the software which are specified as dependencies in&#010;the build specification of the package manager. Debian has dpkg helper&#010;scripts, Fedora has koji and there is also JPackage. It was somewhat&#010;difficult to integrate Maven with the respective package managers and&#010;build systems and for example FreeBSD does not compile Java software and&#010;only uses pre-compiled binaries to avoid these difficulties.&#010;&#010;For other operating systems without package managers, especially&#010;Microsoft Windows and Mac OS X, it is worse. Because all dependencies&#010;have to be bundled with and updated for each independently installed&#010;software. This is particularly problematic for security updates.&#010;&#010;It seems setting up a build service (similar to koji but&#010;platform-independent) that tracks new software versions, is aware of&#010;dependencies between projects and builds all transitive dependencies&#010;from source code with isolated Maven repositories and bundles all&#010;dependencies with the original software. In order to track dependencies&#010;it would be necessary to have adapters that watch and scrap FTP&#010;directories, RSS and atom feeds and websites for updates, import source&#010;code archives, build new releases, rebuild dependent software, flag the&#010;newly build software for testing and approval. While this is certainly&#010;not impossible, it is also not trivial.&#010;&#010;Is anyone aware of a source build system for Maven would meet the&#010;requirements or at least serve as a foundation for building such system?&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Matthias-Christian&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Build once, deploy everywhere  
Date  :-
Wed, 10 Sep 2014 14:03:47 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi All,&#010;&#010;Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method? Like&#010;lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for different&#010;environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. I want to do my compile and package only at&#010;DEV then deploy the artifact to all mentioned environment. Is this possible&#010;using Maven, is there any reference any one could share with me Please.&#010;&#010;  

================

Name  :- 
Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.conno...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Build once, deploy everywhere  
Date  :-
Wed, 10 Sep 2014 14:14:44 GMT  
contents:- 
What you want to do is have your packaged software be independent of the&#010;environment it is deployed to. That way you know by checking the SHA1 of&#010;the artifact you can know it was the one that was tested by QA.&#010;&#010;So what you do is have your application read its configuration from an&#010;external source.&#010;&#010;One example is you could read the configuration from the JNDI environment&#010;(if you are deploying in a JavaEE server). Thus you can setup the dev&#010;environment with the DB servers, etc defined in JNDI and the same for QA,&#010;PROD, etc&#010;&#010;Another example is you could look for a .properties file on the classpath&#010;or at a well known location (perhaps the user home or something like that)&#010;&#010;The application should fail fast if any of the configuration settings are&#010;missing to help diagnose issues.&#010;&#010;There are many ways to skin this cat, but rebuilding an artifact for each&#010;environment should be considered a critical anti-pattern&#010;&#010;On 10 September 2014 15:03, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method? Like&#010;&gt; lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for different&#010;&gt; environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. I want to do my compile and package only at&#010;&gt; DEV then deploy the artifact to all mentioned environment. Is this possible&#010;&gt; using Maven, is there any reference any one could share with me Please.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Re: Build once, deploy everywhere  
Date  :-
Wed, 10 Sep 2014 14:22:28 GMT  
contents:- 
The down side of that is that if your environment details for a specific&#010;server change, then you need to rebuild.&#010;&#010;If you are loading configuration from an external source then you just&#010;update the external source and continue with the app as is.&#010;&#010;On 10 September 2014 15:17, &lt;cody.a.fyler@wellsfargo.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Both of the below are good solutions.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've also seen folks use a run time based solution where a different set&#010;&gt; of properties is loaded based on an Environment Variable common to all&#010;&gt; servers.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cody Fyler&#010;&gt; Lending Grid Build Team&#010;&gt; G=Lending Grid Builds&#010;&gt; (515) – 441 - 0814&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#010;&gt; From: Stephen Connolly [mailto:stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com]&#010;&gt; Sent: Wednesday, September 10, 2014 9:15 AM&#010;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Subject: Re: Build once, deploy everywhere&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What you want to do is have your packaged software be independent of the&#010;&gt; environment it is deployed to. That way you know by checking the SHA1 of&#010;&gt; the artifact you can know it was the one that was tested by QA.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So what you do is have your application read its configuration from an&#010;&gt; external source.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; One example is you could read the configuration from the JNDI environment&#010;&gt; (if you are deploying in a JavaEE server). Thus you can setup the dev&#010;&gt; environment with the DB servers, etc defined in JNDI and the same for QA,&#010;&gt; PROD, etc&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Another example is you could look for a .properties file on the classpath&#010;&gt; or at a well known location (perhaps the user home or something like that)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The application should fail fast if any of the configuration settings are&#010;&gt; missing to help diagnose issues.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There are many ways to skin this cat, but rebuilding an artifact for each&#010;&gt; environment should be considered a critical anti-pattern&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 10 September 2014 15:03, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method?&#010;&gt; &gt; Like lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for&#010;&gt; &gt; different environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. On 10 Sep 2014, at 10:03, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method? Like&#010;&gt; lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for different&#010;&gt; environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. I want to do my compile and package only at&#010;&gt; DEV then deploy the artifact to all mentioned environment. Is this possible&#010;&gt; using Maven, is there any reference any one could share with me Please.&#010;&#010;We do this extensively with maven, using the maven release plugin.&#010;&#010;Our artifacts are in turn installable packages (rpms in our case, but could be deb, whatever)&#010;which get published into a yum repository.&#010;&#010;The code is "promoted" from dev to test to higher environments by hard linking the packages&#010;into distinct yum repos, a yum repo for each environment.&#010;&#010;The release created by the release plugin is built just once and promoted. The rpms are created&#010;using the rpm-maven-plugin.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Graham&#010;--&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi,&#010;&#010;&#010;You can always run mvn deploy:deploy, but the main point of deploy is not&#010;to deploy applications but to deploy binaries into a Maven repository&#010;manager (Nexus ..)&#010;&#010;Deploying applications is traditionnally done via others specifics tools,&#010;though a few maven plugins do that as well.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Sep 10, 2014 at 5:07 PM, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks All.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My package is not environment specific, and currently i compile and package&#010;&gt; using Maven, and run deployment using Ant, coz when i tried to run maven&#010;&gt; deploy it was using the full life cycle goals again, instead of this is&#010;&gt; there any way to execute just deploy and skip all other goals?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Sep 10, 2014 at 9:26 AM, Graham Leggett &lt;minfrin@sharp.fm&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On 10 Sep 2014, at 10:03, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method?&#010;&gt; Like&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for&#010;&gt; different&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. I want to do my compile and package&#010;&gt; only&#010;&gt; &gt; at&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; DEV then deploy the artifact to all mentioned environment. Is this&#010;&gt; &gt; possible&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; using Maven, is there any reference any one could share with me Please.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; We do this extensively with maven, using the maven release plugin.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Our artifacts are in turn installable packages (rpms in our case, but&#010;&gt; &gt; could be deb, whatever) which get published into a yum repository.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The code is "promoted" from dev to test to higher environments by hard&#010;&gt; &gt; linking the packages into distinct yum repos, a yum repo for each&#010;&gt; &gt; environment.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The release created by the release plugin is built just once and&#010;&gt; promoted.&#010;&gt; &gt; The rpms are created using the rpm-maven-plugin.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; &gt; Graham&#010;&gt; &gt; --&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; &gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Adrien Rivard&#010;&#010;

*that* deploy has actually nothing to do with the deploy you want. It's&#010;only and specifically designed to push a binary produced by the building&#010;process to some maven repository manager (say archiva, nexus or artifactory&#010;for example).&#010;&#010;2014-09-10 17:07 GMT+02:00 Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks All.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My package is not environment specific, and currently i compile and package&#010;&gt; using Maven, and run deployment using Ant, coz when i tried to run maven&#010;&gt; deploy it was using the full life cycle goals again, instead of this is&#010;&gt; there any way to execute just deploy and skip all other goals?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Sep 10, 2014 at 9:26 AM, Graham Leggett &lt;minfrin@sharp.fm&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On 10 Sep 2014, at 10:03, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method?&#010;&gt; Like&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for&#010;&gt; different&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. Name  :- 
Jason van Zyl &lt;ja...@takari.io&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Build once, deploy everywhere  
Date  :-
Wed, 10 Sep 2014 15:28:37 GMT  
contents:- 
Yes, this is the only thing I've ever done. Unfortunately all the JEE specs don't seem to be&#010;well thought out in this regard.&#010;&#010;For a given runtime the model I use is one where there is a launcher, a binary part (libs&#010;and app), and configuration. I combine these three things to make a working runtime. I may&#010;launch in an IDE vs a production system (using JSW, daemon tools, shell scripts), and configurations&#010;are going to be different for all environments especially dev vs production, but the binary&#010;part remains constant.&#010;&#010;The launcher for your production environments should be fairly regular as well, so it is really&#010;only your configuration that changes. To deal with configuration I generally package templates&#010;in JARs, and while being extracted I filter them against a known set of variables.&#010;&#010;This is how I construct Facebook's Presto server: https://github.com/facebook/presto/blob/master/presto-server/src/main/provisio/presto.xml&#010;&#010;Under the launcher section there is the configuration as well. We're adjusting how the server&#010;is constructed but you get the idea.&#010;&#010;On Sep 10, 2014, at 10:03 AM, Jan &lt;raghurefer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Does anyone using Maven as Build Once and deploy Everywhere method? Like&#010;&gt; lets say i don't want to recompile my source code everytime for different&#010;&gt; environment DEV,SIT,UAT &amp; PROD. I want to do my compile and package only at&#010;&gt; DEV then deploy the artifact to all mentioned environment. Is this possible&#010;&gt; using Maven, is there any reference any one could share with me Please.&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;believe nothing, no matter where you read it,&#010;or who has said it,&#010;not even if i have said it,&#010;unless it agrees with your own reason&#010;and your own common sense.&#010;&#010; -- Buddha&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.conno...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Maintaining versions in a multi-module project  
Date  :-
Thu, 11 Sep 2014 13:02:32 GMT  
contents:- 
Use whatever works best for you.&#010;&#010;I have some projects where it is better for me to force them all in&#010;lock-step&#010;&#010;I have other projects where I let them run free.&#010;&#010;My general rule of thumb: if the modules are in the same GIT repo or the&#010;same Subversion trunk then they all will end up being released as one&#010;"atomic" group, so keep the version numbers in sync. If they are in&#010;different SCM instances then they will be released independently so let&#010;them run free&#010;&#010;On 11 September 2014 09:35, Anuj Agrawal &lt;anujagrawal83@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I am working on a multi-module project where I see that some of the module&#010;&gt; POMs have versions different from the parent POM. Apparently, developers&#010;&gt; have made changes to some of the modules and updated the version of only&#010;&gt; those modules.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I also see another project where irrespective of which modules have been&#010;&gt; modified, developers modify the versions of all modules using mvn versions&#010;&gt; command to keep all of them in-sync.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am new to maven and have started using it only since last six months.&#010;&gt; Seeing the above mentioned two projects, I am confused what is the right&#010;&gt; path to take - updating all module versions irrespective of where changes&#010;&gt; are, or updating only those module versions where something changed.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Anuj Agrawal&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
[ANN] Apache Maven RAR Plugin Version 2.4 Released  
Date  :-
Thu, 11 Sep 2014 21:00:30 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven RAR Plugin, Version 2.4&#010;&#010;A resource adapter is a system-level software driver that a Java application&#010;uses to connect to an enterprise information system (EIS). The RAR plugin has&#010;the capability to store these resource adapters to an archive (Resource Adapter&#010;Archive or RAR) which can be deployed to a J2EE server.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-rar-plugin&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-rar-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven RAR Version 2.4&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MRAR-28] - Add Support for Classifier&#010; * [MRAR-35] - MavenProject/MavenSession Injection as a paremeter instead as a component.&#010; * [MRAR-37] - Upgrade maven-filtering to 1.2&#010; * [MRAR-38] - Upgrade to Maven 2.2.1 compatiblity&#010;&#010;New Feature:&#010;&#010; * [MRAR-34] - provide "skip" parameter for the plugin&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Tell maven to not have the parent pom as a dependency?  
Date  :-
Fri, 12 Sep 2014 03:25:15 GMT  
contents:- 
I have an OSS module in a multi-module maven project.&#010;&#010;I want to post this to a public repo… it’s open source.&#010;&#010;The problem is that the parent module is not OSS.&#010;&#010;When I setup a &lt;dependency&gt; it pulls in my OSS module just fine, but then&#010;it tries to pull down the parent module, which isn’t in the repo, and&#010;breaks.&#010;&#010;The parent pom isn’t really a dependency… so I’d like it to not need it&#010;&#010;is this possible?&#010;&#010;-- &#010;&#010;Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;… or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Barrie Treloar &lt;baerr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Tell maven to not have the parent pom as a dependency?  
Date  :-
Fri, 12 Sep 2014 05:53:47 GMT  
contents:- 
On 12 September 2014 12:55, Kevin Burton &lt;burton@spinn3r.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have an OSS module in a multi-module maven project.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I want to post this to a public repo… it’s open source.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The problem is that the parent module is not OSS.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; When I setup a &lt;dependency&gt; it pulls in my OSS module just fine, but then&#010;&gt; it tries to pull down the parent module, which isn’t in the repo, and&#010;&gt; breaks.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The parent pom isn’t really a dependency… so I’d like it to not need it&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; is this possible?&#010;&#010;&#010;As Dan says, make it a stand alone project.&#010;i.e. Dont make it a module.&#010;&#010;Being a module has a special meaning - "treat this as part of a bigger&#010;whole".&#010;It also help with syntatic sugar by allowing you to run one command at the&#010;top and have it propogate into all the modules.&#010;&#010;To be complete a module has nothing to do with dependencies or dependency&#010;management.&#010;&#010;The reason your OSS module is pulling in the parent is not because of&#010;dependency, but because of inheritance of the parent hierarchy.&#010;&#010;Usually all modules are released together and will share version&#010;identifiers.&#010;If they are released independently then you normally wont make them&#010;modules, and their version identifiers can do their own thing.&#010;There is a recent post "Maintaining versions in a multi-module project"&#010;that Stephen answers, you might also want to search the archives on this&#010;topic as well.&#010;&#010;A parent pom can be used in two ways; 1) to share common information i.e.&#010;"inheritance" 2) keep related artifacts together to make working on a bug&#010;that traverses artifacts easier i.e "aggregation"&#010;&#010;In your case I dont think you need to use aggregation, you just need to&#010;pull out the OSS artifact into its own stand alone location and then&#010;include it as a normal dependency in your non-OSS project.&#010;&#010;If you find that you are also fixing bugs in the OSS project at the same&#010;time you are working on the non-OSS one, then you might want to create an&#010;aggregate pom that has two modules (one OSS, the other non-OSS) so that you&#010;can run maven commands in one place against both projects. Stephen Connolly&#010;has some stuff somewhere about that I think.&#010;The freely availble Maven books might also go into this in more detail, but&#010;it tends to be a more advanced feature not well described.&#010;&#010;Cheers&#010;Barrie&#010;&#010;

Re: Tell maven to not have the parent pom as a dependency?

contents:- 
The problem I have here is that this would definitely fix my problem.&#010; Breaking it out into another OSS project would be sweet…&#010;&#010;BUT… it would introduce its own set of problems.&#010;&#010;Now I have two projects to maintain.  And the number is increasing… From an&#010;IDE perspective, I have to have N windows and switch between them, and&#010;remember which file is in which project.&#010;&#010;I find it’s 100x easier to just keep everything in one project.&#010;&#010;I could use git-submodules… but IDEA breaks on them and they have a few&#010;gotchas.&#010;&#010;… but perhaps there’s no perfect solution.  Just a few solutions that are&#010;less horrible than my current solution.&#010;&#010;Kevin&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Sep 11, 2014 at 10:53 PM, Barrie Treloar &lt;baerrach@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; On 12 September 2014 12:55, Kevin Burton &lt;burton@spinn3r.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I have an OSS module in a multi-module maven project.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I want to post this to a public repo… it’s open source.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The problem is that the parent module is not OSS.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; When I setup a &lt;dependency&gt; it pulls in my OSS module just fine, but then&#010;&gt; &gt; it tries to pull down the parent module, which isn’t in the repo, and&#010;&gt; &gt; breaks.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The parent pom isn’t really a dependency… so I’d like it to not need it&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; is this possible?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; As Dan says, make it a stand alone project.&#010;&gt; i.e. Dont make it a module.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Being a module has a special meaning - "treat this as part of a bigger&#010;&gt; whole".&#010;&gt; It also help with syntatic sugar by allowing you to run one command at the&#010;&gt; top and have it propogate into all the modules.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; To be complete a module has nothing to do with dependencies or dependency&#010;&gt; management.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The reason your OSS module is pulling in the parent is not because of&#010;&gt; dependency, but because of inheritance of the parent hierarchy.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Usually all modules are released together and will share version&#010;&gt; identifiers.&#010;&gt; If they are released independently then you normally wont make them&#010;&gt; modules, and their version identifiers can do their own thing.&#010;&gt; There is a recent post "Maintaining versions in a multi-module project"&#010;&gt; that Stephen answers, you might also want to search the archives on this&#010;&gt; topic as well.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A parent pom can be used in two ways; 1) to share common information i.e.&#010;&gt; "inheritance" 2) keep related artifacts together to make working on a bug&#010;&gt; that traverses artifacts easier i.e "aggregation"&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In your case I dont think you need to use aggregation, you just need to&#010;&gt; pull out the OSS artifact into its own stand alone location and then&#010;&gt; include it as a normal dependency in your non-OSS project.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you find that you are also fixing bugs in the OSS project at the same&#010;&gt; time you are working on the non-OSS one, then you might want to create an&#010;&gt; aggregate pom that has two modules (one OSS, the other non-OSS) so that you&#010;&gt; can run maven commands in one place against both projects. Stephen Connolly&#010;&gt; has some stuff somewhere about that I think.&#010;&gt; The freely availble Maven books might also go into this in more detail, but&#010;&gt; it tends to be a more advanced feature not well described.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers&#010;&gt; Barrie&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;&#010;Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;… or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Barrie Treloar &lt;baerr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Tell maven to not have the parent pom as a dependency?  
Date  :-
Sat, 13 Sep 2014 01:31:16 GMT  
contents:- 
On 13 September 2014 02:46, Kevin Burton &lt;burton@spinn3r.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; OK… so this definitely works and the aggregation model compiles my module.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But I need a way to bump the version number because I have complex&#010;&gt; dependencies and updating 10 places every time I change the project version&#010;&gt; isn’t going to be fun.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;If you have 10 places where the dependencies need changing you are doing it&#010;wrong.&#010;&#010;You should have zero &lt;version&gt; definitions in your modules.&#010;All version definitions are in the topmost parent pom in the&#010;dependencyManagement section.&#010;If you have a bunch of things that share versions, you can also create a&#010;property and then use something like ${mygroup.version} so that you only&#010;need to update the property section once.&#010;&#010;Have you read the freely available Maven books?&#010;It's been long while since I've read them but I think this advice is in&#010;there.&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Releasing Maven Plugins  
Date  :-
Fri, 12 Sep 2014 12:38:38 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;&#010;I'm currently releasing a new version of Flexmojos. While I sort of found a procedure for&#010;releasing that maven plugin, it's still sort of a PITA.&#010;&#010;&#010;The main problem is that the project contains the plugin as well as some modules that use&#010;the plugin. Now in order to build, I have a "minimal" profile which builds only the plugin&#010;and after that I'm good to go with normal building. Now when doing a release, I usually do&#010;this:&#010;&#010;&#010;- mvn release:prepare (will fail as the plugin doesn't exist in the release version)&#010;&#010;- mvn -Pminimal install (Which installs the release version)&#010;&#010;- mvn release:rollback&#010;&#010;- mvn release:prepare&#010;&#010;- mvn release:perform (will fail as the new SNAPSHOT version of the plugin doesn't exist yet)&#010;&#010;- mvn -Pminimal install (Which installs the SNAPSHOT version)&#010;&#010;- mvn release:perform&#010;&#010;&#010;But to say that's ideal would be a lie ;-)&#010;&#010;&#010;Using version:set to update to the release version and the new SNAPSHOT version and doing&#010;a minimal build of each prior to the actual release, sort of doesn't sound ideal either :-(&#010;&#010;&#010;How do you guys do this when releasing maven plugins?&#010;&#010;&#010;Chris&#010;&#010;&#010;

HI,&#010;&#010; &gt;&#010;&gt; I'm currently releasing a new version of Flexmojos. While I sort of found a procedure&#010;for releasing&#010; &gt; that maven plugin, it's still sort of a PITA.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The main problem is that the project contains the plugin as&#010; &gt;well as some modules that use the plugin.&#010;&#010;This is the basic mistake in this scenario. If you build a maven-plugin &#010;make a separate project from it and do the release etc. only from the &#010;maven-plugin and afterwards you have the release available and can &#010;continue with the rest which uses the release...&#010;&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

&gt;&#010;&gt; The main problem is that the project contains the plugin as&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;well as some modules that use the plugin.&#010;&gt;&#010;This is the basic mistake in this scenario. If you build a maven-plugin&#010;&gt; make a separate project from it and do the release etc. only from the&#010;&gt; maven-plugin and afterwards you have the release available and can continue&#010;&gt; with the rest which uses the release...&#010;&#010;&#010;Although I haven't tried it myself, my understanding is that it should be&#010;possible to use a plugin built within a multi-module project in some of the&#010;other modules when using Maven 3.x. This is not possible with Maven 2.x&#010;though. However, it requires the plugin to be built before the modules that&#010;uses it (which the reactor should be able to calculate, unless there are&#010;some circular module dependencies).&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

If you build a maven-plugin&#010;&gt;&gt; make a separate project from it and do the release etc. only from the&#010;&gt;&gt; maven-plugin and afterwards you have the release available and can  &#010;&gt;&gt; continue&#010;&gt;&gt; with the rest which uses the release...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Although I haven't tried it myself, my understanding is that it should be&#010;&gt; possible to use a plugin built within a multi-module project in some of  &#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; other modules when using Maven 3.x. This is not possible with Maven 2.x&#010;&gt; though. However, it requires the plugin to be built before the modules  &#010;&gt; that&#010;&gt; uses it (which the reactor should be able to calculate, unless there are&#010;&gt; some circular module dependencies).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Kind regards&#010;&gt;&gt; Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Releasing Maven Plugins  
Date  :-
Sat, 13 Sep 2014 09:56:23 GMT  
contents:- 
The root reason is because the "unbuilt" plugin *may* have a custom&#010;lifecycle that affects the reactor build plan in "ways unknown", and that&#010;could end up invalidating the build plan that is being constructed.&#010;&#010;Now the custom lifecycles only come in if a plugin is marked as&#010;&lt;extension&gt;true&lt;/extension&gt; so as long as you are not using a plugin built&#010;in your reactor as an extension we can know that the plugin does not affect&#010;the build plan! and thus we can continue...&#010;&#010;However, IIUC, flexmojos defines custom lifecycles and/or packaging and&#010;thus needs &lt;extension&gt;true&lt;/extension&gt;, and therein is your problem.&#010;&#010;You'll need to split the release process so that the plugin is released&#010;independently&#010;&#010;On Friday, 12 September 2014, Christofer Dutz &lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately I've tried that :-( I can't start the build at all if the&#010;&gt; plugin is not already in the repo as soon as a module intending on using&#010;&gt; the plugin is in reactor.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Chris&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ________________________________________&#010;&gt; Von: Robert Scholte &lt;rfscholte@apache.org &lt;javascript:;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; Gesendet: Freitag, 12. "mvn package” on my code , without tests, is actually pretty fast.  Takes&#010;about one minute.  (I don’t need the tests btw as I’m using continuous&#010;integration and the code is already tested).&#010;&#010;One minute is pretty darn good…&#010;&#010;The problem is that ‘deploy’ takes about 7 minutes.&#010;&#010;That’s kind of not fun.&#010;&#010;I think the issue is that I”m using scpexe for my distributionManagement&#010;repository.&#010;&#010;Any options for improving the performance here?&#010;&#010;I think the issue is creating new SSH connections each time.  I could use&#010;ControlPersist I think… which is an SSH feature to keep the SSH connection&#010;in the background and re-use it.&#010;&#010;Downside: This will require me to use a custom SSH config everywhere.&#010;&#010;Another option is to use a file:// repository which is local and then rsync&#010;the binaries over in one pass.&#010;&#010;Downside: kind of jacky and requires an additional step.&#010;&#010;Any other options ?&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;&#010;Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;… or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&#010;

I could use&#010;&gt; &gt; ControlPersist I think… which is an SSH feature to keep the SSH&#010;&gt; connection&#010;&gt; &gt; in the background and re-use it.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Downside: This will require me to use a custom SSH config everywhere.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Another option is to use a file:// repository which is local and then&#010;&gt; rsync&#010;&gt; &gt; the binaries over in one pass.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Downside: kind of jacky and requires an additional step.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Any other options ?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; --&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;&gt; &gt; Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;&gt; &gt; blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;&gt; &gt; … or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;&#010;Founder/CEO Spinn3r.com&#010;Location: *San Francisco, CA*&#010;blog: http://burtonator.wordpress.com&#010;… or check out my Google+ profile&#010;&lt;https://plus.google.com/102718274791889610666/posts&gt;&#010;&lt;http://spinn3r.com&gt;&#010;&#010;

                   }&#010;                    GlobSelector selector =&#010;                        new GlobSelector( fileset.getIncludes(), fileset.getExcludes(), fileset.isUseDefaultExcludes()&#010;);&#010;
